    <li> Light and creamy! Better than many higher priced products! Would recommend !</li>
    <li> I bought this moisturizer after hearing that Dr. Oz had recommended it, saying that it was the only moisturizer necessary...I assume because of the main ingredient, Collagen Elastin.  I just finished the 10 oz. jar and while it does the job to hydrate my skin at night, I&#x27;m not sure about the long term benefits.  Even though the manufacturer suggests day and night time use, I only use it at night since it doesn&#x27;t have any SPF.</li>
    <li> I Have not had it long so we will see how it works</li>
    <li> Purchased off the reviews but can&#x27;t really tell a difference from this and other face creams, smells nice though</li>
    <li> I was looking for an alternative to a very expensive facial lotion that I had been using. I saw that the rating on this product was very high and I have used some St. Ives products before (apricot scrub, body lotion) and they were fine. This product however is horrible-- I put it on the first day and I like the way it applied and absorbed. The second day was fine, too. The third day, however, I noticed the skin on my nose burned terribly when I applied the lotion. I was somewhat alarmed but the burning subsided and I forgot about it until that evening. I washed my face and the skin on my nose was rough, dry, and scaly. (I had this happen once before when I used a retinol product). I definitely have sensitive skin. Maybe if you don&#x27;t, this product will be fine for you, but if you have any kind of sensitive skin avoid this product!</li>
    <li> I&#x27;m allergic to something in this product which sucks because it really does tighten things up.</li>
    <li> Wonderful moisturizer, Inexpensive and most importantly for me, cruelty free. I alternate it with a higher-end moisturizer for my aging skin. Nice scent, medium texture.</li>

I use daily and have noticed that my skin appears to be more even tone, slight reduction in fine lines. The most significant difference is the noticeably healthy glow that I now have. My skin does not look greasy at all, it looks dewy and fresh. The best part? I will be 50 years old in a few months!! Go St Ives!</li>

My skin texture appearance continues to improve with every use to the point that I always receive unsolicited compliments and I use foundation much more sparingly. The smell is fresh and light.I even use it on my body sometimes! The formula is non-comedogenic, which is essential to someone like me with oily/combination skin type.     <li> I&#x27;ve been using this product for probably 20 years, and I&#x27;m now 64.  I wouldn&#x27;t say it&#x27;s a miracle potion, but my facial skin is mostly wrinkle-free and looks healthy--and I only apply it about every other day.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;FYI, Unilever, one of the consumer product megacorps, now owns St. Ives, and this product has changed. I happen to have an old pre-Unilever jar which states the product is not tested on animals, but the other day, when I bought a new jar at a local pharmacy, I noticed that that claim was gone and there was a Unilever logo in the corner.  So I emailed Unilever asking if the product had been tested on animals, and their response was a link to a web page that contained an awful lot of PR BS about how they&#x27;re trying to evolve into a non-animal testing company, blah blah blah. But no specific information about this moisturizer was offered.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I compared the ingredients in the old jar to the new one, and I noticed that at least three of the natural ingredients are now missing and the order of ingredients has been shuffled.  So for any of you who are experiencing skin irritation, there may be good reason for that.  It&#x27;s not the same product it used to be.  Beware.  I&#x27;m returning my jar to the store I bought it at and I&#x27;ll be looking for an animal-kind moisturizer to replace it.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Please consider writing your representative in Congress to co-sponsor the Humane Cosmetics Act.  The E.U., Israel, Norway, and India have already banned the inhumane and unscientific practice of animal testing on cosmetics. More accurate results can be obtained from human-based cell and tissue testing methods.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;If you want more information on cruelty-free cosmetics, check out, on the NEAVS (New England Anti-Vivisection Society) website, the Coalition for Consumer Information on Cosmetics (CCIC), which certifies more than 500 brands that do not test on animals. Another excellent source is Cruelty Free International, which is a global campaign to end animal testing (more information on NEAVS website). You can watch the video by Ricky Gervais and read about actor Peter Dinklage&#x27;s association with this campaign.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;And did you know that besides being unethical, animal testing produces severe environmental pollution?     <li> I&#x27;m a 28 year old male, with thin, sensitive skin.  My complexion is clear and mostly smooth with larger pores on my cheeks on either side of my nose.  In warmer months, I have normal to oily skin and, in colder months, I have tight, dry skin, especially around my chin, nose, and forehead.  I am a smoker.  When I turned 18, I had my first major experience with dry skin.  At the time, I was bathing with a bar of soap, including my face.  I developed a red, flaky rash around my chin and upper lip that winter, which was embarrassing.  I had no idea why it occurred and went to the doctor, who prescribed antibiotics and steroids which did very little.  In fact, using the steroids for more than a few weeks caused steroid induced dermatitis everywhere it had been applied.  I began using Spectro Jel and then Cetaphil exclusively on my face (and body wash to bathe), and the rash faded and never returned.  Within the last couple of years, I&#x27;ve simply been using a sensitive skin body wash tailored for my body and face with no problems - usually either Dove Men or Nivea.  Still, every winter, I develop tight, dry skin, which is mildly flaky (but not rashy, like before) around my chin, nostrils, and between my eyebrows.  The creases around my nostrils and upper lip also become slightly red, like wind burn.  I decided to try a moisturizer with some reluctance because I&#x27;ve always been afraid that adding anything to my face that isn&#x27;t a cleanser will cause a break out.  I&#x27;ve had bad luck in the past with moisturizers doing this and ultimately why I swore them off for years.  Sensitive skin is a gift and a curse.  On one hand, my skin is very soft and smoothly textured; on the other, it&#x27;s hard to balance the need to cleanse to prevent blemishes and the need to moisturize so dry skin doesn&#x27;t occur.  I bought this product based on reviews, which is always a gamble.  So far, I am very satisfied.  The moisturizer is light and once it goes on it does not feel heavy on the face.  The odoris slightly medicinal but does not linger when applied.  My face is feeling moisturized and supple.  Problem areas, especially the outsides of my nostrils which are always the tightest, are no longer dry, tight, and flaky.  I haven&#x27;t experienced any reddening, either.  No blemishes so far - I have been applying the moisturizer for the past 4-5 days.  Even the creases on either side of my mouth seem filled in and smooth - I always thought &amp;#34;fine line repair&amp;#34; was advertising fluff for older, wrinkly women wanting to look young again.  I will update in the future.  So far, so good.  **Update - 5/6/15** I have unfortunately downgraded my rating to three stars.  I used the moisturizer sporadically over this past winter.  The honeymoon period - when I made my original 5-star review - quickly wore off.  While this product does moisturize well, it started to cause blemishes for me, even with light use.  It does not irritate my skin but it clearly clogs my pores.  So, for those with oily or combo skin and prone to blemishes, I would not recommend this.</li>

I like that it has clean, safe ingredients too - I noticed a few reviews from people complaining about certain ingredients and spreading false info. I&#x27;ve personally researched every ingredient in this moisturizer (as I do every product I put on my skin or in my body), and I just felt I should set the record straight.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(1) Cosmetic and pharmacological grade mineral oil is completely different from industrial mineral oil (which is what many people try to scare you with). It is highly refined to allow skin to breathe while at the same time creating a protective barrier on skin, locking in moisture. It is one of the safest, most effective and most gentle moisturizers known to man. It does not cause cancer, damage your liver or age skin - all those claims are from misinformed people who confuse it with unrefined industrial mineral oil. The two are totally different.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;(2) Propylene Glycol is a humectant and delivery agent. It is very safe and used in minuscule amounts in cosmetic products. It helps bring the active ingredients in a product down deep into the skin where they can be utilized for the skin&#x27;s benefit.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I am more than a little tired of the scare tactics used by some overzealous but misinformed people about perfectly safe ingredients. People, please don&#x27;t listen to every scary person or website, but do your own research. Consider valid, medical affiliated websites with actual accountability and peer reviewed information, NOT the websites that are more like blogs by fear-mongers, or websites designed to sell their own &amp;#34;natural&amp;#34; products.
